=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Very much depends on the group being played, but a combination of factors led to me not liking this game.

* beginner rules have you shuffle your hand+discard+undrawn cards each round, resulting in no guarantee that all cards are seen (I never drew marshall cards, and only had 2 horizontal movement cards all game)
* Belle's ability is very strong in a 5-player game
* Early rounds make a huge difference with bullet cards being doled out and affecting every following turn

The randomness of the game also led to constraints, such as lack of early movement means limited targets and severely limited loot options, and spending an action to draw more cards left you as a sitting duck.

Would not need to own, and would not seek to play again.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Tricky up front, but who can resist those little cardboard trains? The meeples and treasure pieces work so well with it. 

This is a "program your moves" kind of game, but what I like about that is when it's time for you to execute a desired move, you still have flexibility to tweak it just a little bit. A "run" can mean run into a car in front of OR behind you, a "climb" can mean climb up on to OR down into a car. Want to shoot or punch someone? You may have unexpected choices there, too. 

I love the randomness of things going slightly wrong and the domino effect that results. We did miss the first few "special events" that happened on account of the easy-to-miss, small icons on each round card, and the rules did take some time to decipher up front.

That said, my expectations were really high, but they weren't quite met (especially for a SdJ winner-- but doesn't that happen with any awarded game?). The folks I played with had a decidedly "reserved" vibe about them. I need more plays to determine if this is stronger or weaker.

Positives
- Yes, I do love gimmicks, and the train cars are worthwhile ones
- Flexibility in executing a programmed move can help recover from an unforeseen "accident" that occurs before you can move
- Lots of random shooting, punching and looting-- over the top silliness

Negatives
- Rules can be a bit intimidating to newcomers, but they'll get it after one game
- Shooting mechanic doesn't really make sense-- getting shot should be a much more brutal occurrence but it just slows you down a little
- People who love rules over chaos may get frustrated with this one
- It can sometimes be a little tricky to pull or place your characters and treasure tiles out of or into the little cars
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I played this game just once, so these are mostly impressions that may change after multiple plays.

Another solid choice for the Spiel des Jahres. First of all the visual impact of the game is great! The artwork, the 3D train, the meeples... everything is just beautiful when it's set up on the table. The theme is not one of my favorites, but it's nice and I guess that it would work very well in a family setting.

The game-play, while maybe nothing really innovative, is crazy and fun. I like the solution of putting the cards in a communal pile and flipping it at the end to resolve the programming... it makes everything run so smooth! I also like the fact that every round is a little different thanks to the cards, which introduce every time a small new mechanism to the game-play. Of course there's really not much strategy and depth in Colt Express, but on the other hand the game offers a great deal of chaos, excitement and craziness instead!

All together Colt Express is a great family game. It does everything right to be a perfect fit for that setting: it's easy to play, it's beautiful, it's exciting and it's quick enough to be played a couple of times in a row. The Spiel des Jahres committee really couldn't make a better choice. I like this game a lot!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
[b]26.11.2014 - after 1 play[/b]
COLT EXPRESS is a game set in a Wild West background, with players taking the roles of bandits, trying to steal as much money as possible from a running train. Each character has a unique ability and every player has the same action cards that are used in order to "program" their moves.

The thing that makes this game stand out (literally) is the 3D cardboard train, that acts as a spatial gameboard, on which players make their moves. Although the card stock for the cards is flimsy, the train is made from sturdy cardboard and has a potential for capturing the attention of people not playing the game.

By using this "gizmo", the theme is integrated well into the game, as players can ride on top of the train, shoot from a cart to another or ride the engine.

Gameplay wise, it is a game of backstabbing, guessing and counter-guessing, in which the level of luck is very high. The fun factor is also high, as you might find yourself doing things that you never thought you would do, because of the continuous change of the game. Because of these, some players could not like it and refuse to play it a second time.

+ The train "board"
+ Light and funny
- Too much luck for some
- Poor Cardstock for cards
- The "Gunslinger" title ($1000 for the one that uses the most bullets) seems overpowered

I may play it again if in the right mood
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.5
Welche Karten aus meinem Kartensatz habe ich diese Runde zur Verfügung?
Was mache ich mit denen?
Planung? Mit sicherer Aussicht auf Erfolg planen kann nur der Startspieler seinen ersten Zug. Danach besteht die Planungsphase meist in Reaktionen. Handlungsabfolgen kann man sich vornehmen, ob das aber klappt, hängt davon ab, was sonst so passiert. Zwischendurch werden in der Planungsphase Karten verdeckt gespielt, da kann man nur zu ahnen versuchen. Manches, was man gerne gemacht hätte, kann man schon in der Planungsphase vergessen, weil man die dafür nötigen Karten in dieser Runde gar nicht hat. 
In der Aktionsphase läuft dann nur noch ab, was in der Planungsphase angedacht war. Da gibt es überraschende Entwicklungen und man findet sich an einem Ort, an dem man gar nicht sein wollte, so dass man eine Aktion nicht oder anders zu spielen hat, als es mal geplant war.
Ein eher lustiges Chaos mit einem Ende, das sehr stark vom Zufall beeinflusst ist.

In meinem Solospiel zum Kennenlernen hat durch seinen letzten Zug, der doch tatsächlich ausführbar war, der Spieler gewonnen, der zwischendrin im Mittelfeld lag, im konkreten Zeitpunkt aber letzter war.

Ein Spiel für Zocker, absolut nichts für Optimierer.

RATING: 7.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A toyish programmed action game wherein you move from train car to train car, or on top of the train, in order to pick up loot.  You can also punch, shoot, or move a sheriff, to disrupt other player's plans. There is a modicum of deck building in the game such that when you are shot, your deck gets filled with worthless bullet cards. 

Like a more involved, three dimensional "Walk the Plank" (which seemed slightly more fun for me if I recall), this is a worthy design for what it seeks to accomplish: toyish fun with programmed actions in an amusing setting.

I can readily see how this game would appeal to children, perhaps boys of a certain age in particular, but for my present adult tastes, this is just not a game that I want to be play again, so must give it a 6 at best.

RATING: 8.7
Variable player powers, variable round effects, programmed actions, and an amazing 3D visual space to tinker it. Colt Express is goofy yet thematic, as your Bandits attempt to steal loot and get in one anothers' way. Lots of neat little mechanics here, like when you shoot another Bandit you give them a Bullet card they have to shuffle into their Action deck, which can end up with them having less Actions on their turn. The game is just zany fun, and I'm sad I resisted it for as long as I did.

RATING: 6.5
A lot of laughs for your buck. Of course there's little match between the real world and what goes on here in cardboard land - but that doesn't matter much because this is not an attempt to wargame a Wild West era train robbery. For instance, you can't shoot people in the same carriage as you, you have to walk up to them and punch them. You can however shoot people in the next carriage even though you couldn't see them. You keep getting shot but never die. You can be punched and shot while running on the roof of the moving train but never fall off. This is cartoon Wild West and not meant to be taken seriously. For the same reason it is probably pointless to complain that there's a fair dose of luck (in my last game I played Cheyenne, whose special ability is punching, but I only drew my punch card once). When played as a lighthearted hour of fun, it works just fine.
Update: I wouldn't use the character special abilities, they are wildly unbalanced.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Colt Express has very cool theme and components, and it is also a very fun game!

The basic mechanic is a card-based programming à la Robo Rally, but with the actions chosen one after the other (and not at the same time) and open (but some actions, taken in tunnels, are played face down).
As soon as players complete programming, the actions are performed, and there is some thrill and much fun!

This game is quite easy to grasp, and I guess it can be enjoyed even by non gamers. Even more if you play it while listening to some Ennio Morricone's soundtrack!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4
Ameritrashy theme and components with a half-Euro, half-Ameritrash mechanical system.

The separation of the playing of and resolving of cards seems unnecessary and a wasted opportunity to make it matter more. Perhaps a first-in, last-out type system (a la M:TG) could have been developed into a more interesting game.

There is so much 'take-that' that the only winning strategy seems to be to use all of your bullets and gain the Gunslinger bonus, while hoping that you can end the game with one or two pieces of loot.

RATING: 5
After repeated plays, I have found Colt Express rather disappointing. I appreciate a chaotic, programmed movement game as much as the next guy. The problem I find is that the interaction seems harder to come by than I ever expected. After the first few cards it's tough to keep track of where everyone is located so punching and shooting becomes a random guessing game. Even when played with different groups of people, including those who think out their moves extensively it hasn't work for me. Also all the money tends to get snatched up early, so it becomes a strange chase around the train looking to punch people. My expectations are always elevated with Spiel des Jahres winners and this one didn't live up.

RATING: 7.8
Juego de asaltar un tren. Cada jugador lleva a un bandolero y su objetivo es robar la mayor cantidad de dinero del tren antes de que llegue a la estación. Se juega en cinco turno. En cada turno, una carta indica cuantas rondas se juegan. En cada ronda, un jugador puede jugar una carta de acción, o robar tres cartas de su mazo. Una vez que todos han jugado sus rondas, se resuelve el turno y van sucediendose las acciones en el orden que se jugaron las cartas. Es caótico totalmente y ahí precisamente reside su gracia. Algunas veces las cartas se juegan bocaabajo. Para más coña, al final de cada ronda hay un evento. Es un juego divertido y apto para todo el mundo. Bastante rápido.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Slightly odd game. It's been called a programming game, but it's not really, since the great majority of cards are played openly. It's really a memory/tactical game, and it's mostly about doing the best you can with a constrained set of options. Not quite sure what to make of it - it clearly wants to be a fun, light-ish action game, but then it can't offer you the appropriate set of decisions to evoke that feel. You spend most of your time doing look-ahead, recapping sequences of card plays, and then making fairly trivial tactical choices. The right answer, for the purpose of delivering on the game's apparent design intent, seems to be to offer you more decisions about risk and bluff. Instead there is this weird dynamic where it's primarily an extremely straightforward tactical look-ahead game, but one where occasional mistakes, misrememberings, or wrong analyses can have catastrophic consequences (rendering your entire turn ineffective). If the game were more sensible you would have to make a lot of guesses over the course of the game and things would go wrong with some frequency; instead, since it's mostly a tactical analysis game, you get rare missteps having huge downside consequences.

Anyway, this analysis is somewhat immaterial because really there is almost no game on offer here. Choices are mostly completely obvious, tactics are trivial, and there is very little (and often no) element of bluff or deception. I think it would be a totally entertaining game to play with mixed groups of younger kids and adults, or kids of various age ranges, but for purely adult gamers there is almost nothing on offer here beyond the generic appeal of playing a game (this is not nothing, certainly. But there are a lot of actual good games).

For the record, I think the "advanced" game (where you can retain cards from turn to turn) may actually be wrong. I've only played once so this is just a general principles/design aesthetic argument, but the additional control may actually not be desirable, given the game is what it is. The more that players can do something close to what they want, the more their actions become predictable and so the overall effect is to make the game kind of boring. When players start doing oddball stuff because their turns are heavily constrained, the game as a whole - when measured as an experience for everyone - becomes more interesting (even though it might suck to be an overly constrained player). Also, since it's mostly a game of triumphing over constraint, moderating the level of constraint removes the only real key design element and can deny the player a sense of accomplishment when the constraints are overcome.

OK, that was more words than this design really deserved. I don't think this is a particularly interesting design, certainly not artful in any way and of little interest to the hobbyist gamer.

The game it sort of reminds me of is Infiltration - the games have very surprisingly similar aesthetics and goals although Infiltration is obviously targeting a quite different demographic. But Infiltration is at least executed with some artistry.

RATING: 7
A pretty neat pre=programmed movement game, where all players play cards onto a common pool, attempting to move around the train, attack the other players, and pick up sweet loot.  Then all of those cards are played out in the order they were played.

This would all be kind of boring if not for a bit of introduced randomness that keeps the proceedings from being entirely predictable!  Every once in a while, the train enters a tunnel, which means cards are played face down for one turn.  There are also a few other elements that keep things from being a sure thing.

Overall, good, light and kind of silly. The 3D train is also a cool gimmick that makes it more enjoyable than it probably should be!

RATING: 7
This is a quick programmed movement game where each bandit during a train robbery is trying to beat up the other players, hide from the marshal and grab as much loot as possible during the 5 rounds. What sets it over the top is the awesome 3D train components. Each round has players adding 3-5 action cards (move, punch, climb, steal, etc) in turn order to a stack, that are then revealed. Best laid plans are soon foiled as the player you thought you were punching is now a few cars away and instead the marshal is shooting at you as you scramble to the roof. It plays quick (30-40 mins) and if you embrace the chaos, it is a lot of fun.

RATING: 7.4
This most recent SdJ winner is enjoyable but not as fun as it could be. The components all look great and the idea is solid, it just stumbles a bit in the execution.

In CE you take the plan-ahead element from games like RoboRally and then wait to see where the players end up. Find yourself in the same car as another player and you'll have a chance to take a shot at them, or steal their dough. The biggest problem I noticed is that the special powers each player gets are very unbalanced. A few may never get used, while others are consistently handy.

I would play this again if asked, but I'm glad I got to try it first to confirm it's not one I need in my collection. And I think the SDJ folks got it wrong this time - both Machi Koro and The Game were more deserving.

RATING: 9
A crazy game of trying to rob a train, shoot your opponents and not encounter the Marshal.

Players pick their actions in sequence by placing cards in a central pile, then it's flipped over and the actions are gone through one at a time.

Have you remembered what others placed and played accordingly, or are you now trying to steal loot already gone or shoot somebody who is no longer in view?

Not sure I've ever won this game, but have thoroughly enjoyed every play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
It takes an experienced gamer only one play to know if they'll like Colt Express or not. I myself seem to love any game with a pre-programming mechanic, so I would have been shocked if I hadn't enjoyed this one immediately. But I've learned that games with pre-planned actions having the possibility of going awry isn't everyone's cup of tea.

To my mind, all the comparisons to Roborally are quite off-base because the programming in Colt Express has a unique twist in that the play of action cards happen sequentially as it's emerging, allowing you to somewhat react and adjust to the situation while it unfolds before your eyes and imagination...assuming you can correctly envision the movie-reel antics that are about to ensue, let alone even have the cards in hand to do anything about it. This makes the expert variant of this game somewhat of a necessity, if only to offset potentially brutal card draws comprised of nothing but bullets while your neighbors draw exactly what they need.

I feel this is a great family game, but also feel it's just a tad beyond the gateway level.

Update: Finally got to play it with my family and it bombed pretty hard. So sad. Oh well, I still love it, so need to be creative in finding ways to get it to a table somehow.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A great game.  Don't take it too seriously or you'll be upset!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.8
Very nice and funny concept for a game, involving action planning and a 3D board (this case, a train).
The action planning associated with hand management (and some memory)is the great challenge of this game, also providing some funny (or frustating) moments, as some (most)of the actions you planned are often no longer possible, due to the actions of other players (from which you only can guess very few). However, it´s sometimes possible to do actions you never thought of...
The (automatic) mechanics of the game (refills, deals, etc)can be a little heavy, especially for a party game, but it´s still a fine experience, if you don´t have too high expectations for an hour of play.

Party programming game with a light hearted western theme of train robbing. Everyone programs several moves open handed but the twist is that a set of moves can potentially be hidden.

Goal is straightforward, just grab the most loot. Turn order is very powerful and important to planning. Being left alone by players and offensive sheriff control means victory. Random card draw can hurt despite draw mechanism.

Good quality components with the wild west meeples and 3D train board. Probably best for families or as a gateway game.

RATING: 9
This game is a great casual game. Lots of fun, and easy to get to the table (2-6 players, easy to teach, not abstract, and short setup/play time). It's been a hit with everyone I've played with so far, and I can't get enough myself.
The sweet spot for strategic play seems to be 3 or 4 players, beyond that it tends to turn into a bit of a brawl (which is just as fun as long as you adjust expectations).
The expert mode variant (basically, keeping your hand between rounds and shuffling your draw deck only when it is empty, instead of cycling your hand and shuffling every round) I think could help bring a more strategic experience at all player levels, but I've only played it in 2 player thus far.

RATING: 6
Simple programming game, where players are train robbers looting a moving train.  A nicely implemented, chaotic family game where players take turns adding action cards to a deck, which is regularly flipped and resolved.  Actions include moving up and down the lovely 3-D train "game board", either along the carriages or roof, punching and shooting their opponents, and looting the carriages of cash/gem chips.  Most loot at the end of five rounds wins.  Chaotic, slightly fiddly with the tiny carriages, but good for what it is.

A játékosok minden fordulóban megtervezik (hol nyíltan, hol titkosan) mit szeretnének végrehajtani az adott fordulóban, majd az akció fázis során megpróbálják megvalósítani a terveiket, amibe a többi játékos rendszeresen beleszól és ebből adódnak a vicces szituációk: levegőbe bokszolás és lövöldözés, marsall elől menekülés, stb. Az édesapámnak sikerült olyan helyzetbe kerülnie, amikor egy ékszer megszerzése helyett először el kellett menekülnie a marsall elől a tetőre, aki azért egy lövést még utána küldött, majd mivel a tetőn éppen Ő volt az egyetlen akire lehetett lőni, ezért gyorsan bekapott még egy lövést, majd visszavonult a vonatfülkébe búsan, mivel egy értékes kincs helyett sikerült neki két lövést is begyűjtenie :). A 3d-s vonat nagyon látványos, bár nagyobb ujjakkal kissé nehézkes lehet a bábuk mozgatása. Vicces helyzeteket kedvelő családoknak kifejezetten ajánlott. (2017.12.27.)

RATING: 8
 This is the second programmable-move game to come out of Essen, the other being the highly entertaining Lords of Xidit.  And Colt Express is also a great ride.   It isn’t quite as tense and exciting as Xidit but it has the benefit of playing in a third of the time and fitting a lot of laughs and entertainment along the way. 

The model train and the theme work really well: the characters riding atop of the train or in the carriage, fighting other characters, shooting them, stealing from them and so on.  Being a programmable move game there are plenty of times when a thrown fist  simply hits the fresh air, or when a shot is fired with no one to shoot at.  

All-round family and light gamery entertainment at its best.

RATING: 6.5
I was walking by a game being setup and was invited to play.  After the cardboard train came out to the table, I was intrigued.

The premise is great and I like the idea of train robbery for a theme, and while there is nothing wrong or unlikeable about the game, I don't think it's an exceptional entry to the hobby.  For something so visually and thematically appealing, I was a bit disappointed to learn that the main mechanic of the game was programming.  While it proved to be interesting, especially with the face-down "tunnel" portions of the programming sequence to keep you guessing, I think if I want to play something like this, I'll go with Lords of Xidit or Space Alert.

Still, if action programming is your cuppa, there's nothing here that will disappoint you.  Couple that with, say, Trains' trash cards clogging your deck, and you've pretty much got the idea.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.88
Cutthroat, Light

Has surpassed King of New York as my groups go-to light "take that!" game.  No dice rolling so each person feels somewhat more in control of what they are doing, plenty of direct conflict, it plays reasonably fast, no player elimination and it rewards good strategy.  It's very easy to teach (after one practice round, players will get it) and even beginners usually aren't blown out unless they get shot a bunch.  I think Ghost and Belle are overpowered but not egregiously so.  Being able to play that first card face down gives Ghost a huge edge, same goes for Belle not being able to be targeted if there are other valid targets.  Still, would bring this out every time we got new players or slow learners.  Considering the expansions but I don't want to over complicate this game, it's beauty is in it's simplicity.

RATING: 7.5
I was a little quick judging this game. It is really fun when your programmed moves really pay off and also when your and other plans really do NOT pay off:)
It is a good family game with a lot of laughter and surprising outcomes.
However, there are three things that bother me with this game. The 3D cars are way too small, so it's almost impossible to pick the pieces and tokens out of them. It would have been better with just a 2D game board. I wonder if it had won SdJ if they had decided to go for 2D. I believe not, and that's a problem (maybe for the gaming industry). The other thing is that some players (that get a lot of bullets) may draw a hand that is really worth nothing. Of course, you can use one turn drawing 3 cards, but it feels like waste.
The third thing is that I don't think it works well with 2-3 players. The differences in score are often too much, and there are not so much action going on, despite the fact that you play with fewer cards.
Rating has gone significantly up since my first experience, so that's a good sign:)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Great all around game! Great theme, really fun play style.  You get a personal deck of cards that have actions on them. You draw a hand from your deck.  Then you take turns placing a card in a pile from the ones in your hand, sometimes face down.  When everyone has played their cards, some of them face down sometimes, you flip the whole pile over and play out the actions in turn.  Most of the time, you see what others have played, so you can strategize.  The fun happens when cards are placed face down, so you don't know what anyone else is doing.  This means that you might wind up shooting at someone on top of the train who climbed down into a car just a turn before, or punching air because someone vacated the car you were in.  Or one player moves into range of your gun, and your intended target moves out of it, and you wind up accidentally shooting the other guy instead.

RATING: 7
I don't know, I'm torn on this game. The components are fantastic. The 3-D trains and cacti are amazing. Yet the gameplay felt a little less enjoyable then I would have hoped. Played it two players, and set up and rules run through was tough. There's only five rounds which didn't seem like enough. Grabbing (and holding onto) purses and gems was difficult as there aren't that many cards in your personal deck to do that. A house rule of a few more rounds might be needed. The only complaint I have with the components is that the train cars are not high enough. Placing and moving your characters around almost always results it knocking something over. Overall it was okay. I'm giving it an 8.5 based mostly on design. I know it will get more play time, so hopefully it will grow on me. 

Traded 9/2/16.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Light-Hearted, quick programming game. While I've played with three and four players, I think the game would be best played with 5 or 6 due to how hectic the game would become. Component quality of the train and cards is great, but the player boards are made of a thin card-like material that peels easily. It would have been nice if these were made of cardboard, or at least a thicker, more protective material.

There's potential in the game for someone to be completely ruined by bad luck or decisions - adding bullet cards that clog up a player's hand with worthless cards. This mechanic is thematic, and the game balances this by allowing players to spend a turn to draw three additional cards. Additionally, games are short so if a player makes a series of bad decisions he or she can get back into the game after only 30 minutes.

RATING: 6
Colt Express is a silly little game. There is so much player-induced chaos, both deliberate and incidental, that It's hard to take seriously. The over-the-top 3D train "board" probably serves to reinforce that impression even more. Even though Colt Express often gets compared to RoboRally, there is quite a bit less programming and similarly reduced influence here. At the same time, it runs quite a bit shorter.

If you are looking for some strategic heist planning you better go look somewhere else. However, as a quick "in-your-face" romp where the ride is more important than the final result Colt Express certainly has its moments.

RATING: 7
COLT EXPRESS simuliert einen Raubüberfall auf eine Lokomotive im Wilden Westen und glänzt dabei von einer thematischen Unmittelbarkeit und Wunderbarkeit, die das Spiel zu einer wilden, anarchischen Ballerei und Balgerei macht. Das Spielprinzip ist so simpel wie ein Stetson: Karten mit Aktionen aus Rennen, Schiessen, Hüpfen, Schlagen, Klauen auf einen Stapel legen, offen und blind, und nacheinander runterspielen. Daraus ergibt sich ein rasantes, unkalkulierbares Chaos auf dem herzallerliebsten, dreidimensionalen Zug, in dessen Wagons sich Wurstfinger und Grobiane vergeblich mühen dürfen. COLT EXPRESS ist Rauchende Colts, ist mehr Spielzeug als Spiel, aber als solches von romantischer, jungenhafter Verzückung.

RATING: 8
Lately, I have not been playing enough to tell whether this game is a worthy SdJ winner. However, I would guess so.

I do not take the game seriously. I do my stuff, sometimes they work, often they don't. I have only played the game a few times, and the winner never knew how they have won. (Including myself.) The characters are definitely not balanced and the more players you have, the less control you have on how the whole thing will go. (I have played this with 4 and 6.)

Nevertheless, I have no problem with this. I enjoy watching how the chaos unravels every turn. I am always pretty happy if I manage to sneak my idea through, but never really mind if I don't. Basically, I am always involved, but I'm only rarely frustrated - that's an awesome combo. I also do not know too many other games, where the players actually laugh when something gets messed up. In a friendly environment this is a definitely good choice for a short game.

Update: I bump this to an 8 (from 7). I have played it with a bunch of people new to boardgames and they loved it. The theme is awesome which makes it easy to get involved. The rules are super easy and they could grasp them immediately. And once again, we laughed throughout all the games. I would definitely get bored with Colt Express if I had to play it more often - it does not have any hidden depths or anything. (I only play it ~annually so I don't mind that.) However, it is more of a gateway game and is also an incredibly well-designed one.

RATING: 8
After a few plays I love this game.  I am sure there are flaws I am overlooking in favor of the killer components (3D cardboard train!!!) so forgive me.

The game exudes theme and is full of exciting gameplay.  There is enough variants in the rulebook to play this game with any audience.  I have played with groups of kids under 8 and with groups mixed kids and adults.  It is very simple to drop or add the more advanced rules.

On top of having flexibility in specific rules; there is also a well thought out 2-player rule variant.

My only complaint with the rulebook is the lack of clarity on setting up the train (it really lays it out like it is supposed to be in a specific order when it does not) and secondly there is not clear guidance that once the action deck is built that it should be hidden and revealed one at a time (i.e. players can't look into the deck to see what is coming next... they need to be forced to remember what was played).

Other than those two clarifications in the rules I plan to play this on a regular basis.  Shooting and moving and the excitement of seeing what players played in secret during the tunnel rounds makes for a great session!

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
(01/02/2015) Comment based on 1 play.

This is a humorous, but well executed take on Robo Rally, constrained to a one-dimensional line (forwards and aftwards), stacked (constrained to two levels), with some combat and treasure collection, driven by a deck-building (clogging?) mechanism.

First off, the physical components are well made, especially the cardboard 3D representation of the steam locomotive and passenger cars. It actually feels like a moderate miniatures game, with very crude movement and combat.

Starting with a deck of ten action cards, each player draws six randomly to form their hand. In turn order, they "program" their actions in a first-in/first-out queue. The actions are the expected fore/aft movement, climb up/climb down, fire gun, punch, pick up treasure (money, which is VP), or move the marshal. There are five "acts", with each act dictating four or five actions per player, along with some interesting plot twist at the end. Further, one of the four/five action slots is a "tunnel", which allows players to program an action face-down; normally, actions are programmed face-up, so others can react accordingly.

Programming face-up actions can be predictable and boring, but the one hidden action can throw unpredictability into the mix, making a mess of all the players' plans--the result is a hysterical narrative of plans going terribly wrong. It is within this chaotic framework that players are trying to collect as much treasure (with hidden values) scattered throughout the train. Also, each player role has a special power that can add more unpredictability!

The novel feature is as players shoot each other, they give the victim a useless "bullet" card that is shuffled into the victim's deck! As the victim takes more hits, the more their deck gets clogged, like Curses in Dominion. The wandering marshal also hands out bullets to clog up decks. The player that successfully shoots the most bullets wins a game-end bonus. After five acts, whomever has the most money wins the game.

All in all, this is a light-hearted, fast-paced game, full of hilarious outcomes, but surprisingly meaty in terms of tactics. It is an excellent 30-minute romp, very thematic (if you like spaghetti Westerns), and a very engaging good time. Lastly, it is very accessible to both gamers and non-gamers alike, as well as adults and younger children. It is a solid "7", with possible bump up to an "8" with more plays.

(01/03/2015) 2 plays. First 6-player game was rather chaotic, with so many players crawling all over the train. Still, a fun romp, holding at a steady "7". It looks rather trivial in terms of mechanics, but it provides a good mix of randomness, mitigated by skillful foresight and planning.

RATING: 9
Colt Express is one of those games where you can have a great time even if you're not doing very well, score-wise. Trying to guess what other players are choosing to do can be a great challenge and I particularly enjoy trying to come up with flexible strategies which can change my turn on-the-fly. Plus, 3D cardboard train!

It's a very different experience with 3 players than with 6. Smaller player numbers make it easier to keep track of card placement and possible intentions, 6 players makes it almost impossible to keep in mind everybody's movements and leads to much more defensive play.

RATING: 4.7
I had high hopes for this game following all of the accolades it received.  Unfortunately, Colt Express fell flat for my game group.  Admittedly, I prefer deep strategy games - but this game was not enjoyable (for me) even as a light filler game.  The programming mechanism is intriguing, but in practice the game is far too random for my tastes.  Players can have entire rounds (there are 5 rounds) where they accomplish nothing and those players that do make progress do so almost entirely because of chance, which, in my opinion, removes the fun.  The randomness and luck make this feel more like a young children's game, but I wouldn't feel comfortable introducing this to young children due to the robbery and gun violence themes.  I can see the how this game will be enjoyable for some, but it is not for me.  The artwork and component quality, however, are top notch.

Weighted Rating: 4.7 (Fun 3; Gameplay 3; Components 10; Theme 6)
Formula:
[Weighted rating = (((Fun*4) + (Gameplay*3) + (Components *2) + (Theme *1))/10)]

RATING: 3
Colt Express wastes a great theme and components on a game filled with decisions that can be rendered meaningless through plays made randomly by other players. The game hides entirely too much information (the tunnels instantly turn rounds into guessing games) and doesn't even always allow an attempt at an optimal move thanks to only having some of a player's actions available at any given time.

Some might enjoy the chaos of playing this game; I find the restrictions it imposes overly limiting and, not merely devoid of fun, but annoying.

RATING: 6
2015-11-19

Initial Rating: 6.0 (November 2015)

I wasn’t expecting much from the game, but I was pleasantly surprised by it, that is, I had lots of fun playing it. I still think the game needs a good group to be properly enjoyed but I’m open to play it again in the near future.

The game components are awesome and they really add to the thematic setting. The theme is ok I guess, it is a bit boring for me, but it shines through the game.

The game´s rules are very easy to teach and the playtime is around 45 minutes.

There is a fair share of luck in Colt Express, but in this case I don’t mind as much as the game plays so quickly, for the same reason I don’t mind the “attack the perceived leader” factor present in it. Each player has a different role and each role has a power. Many of these powers seem unbalanced and situational but again, I don´t mind because the game is light and quick. You can always balance it with the players´ actions.

I think you need at least 4 players to enjoy the game. 

Bottom line, I think Colt Express is a great family game, it offers lots of fun in a short timeframe. I would play again if requested but I already sold my copy of the game.

RATING: 1
Colt Express works by preprogramming your moves using cards drawn from a deck of basic actions, such as shoot, walk and so on. Your moves are programmed with random draws and if you're shot, do nothing cards are shoved in to your deck. You have little control over your own actions, and even less so of other players. Regardless of how it's packaged, this game is just a group of people picking cards at random and then seeing what happens. I didn't think i'd ever think a game could have too much interaction, but Colt Express certainly proved me wrong. This game is an absolute mess. It has a cardboard train though, so it flies off the shelf.

RATING: 7.8
Played a few games now and I have enjoyed them but now I'm getting to know the game a little bit I feel the rounds are just a little to short. If you find yourself out of position on the last round you might have no options available to you at all. The fun of the game is definitely predicting the other players moves and messing them up but the game can depend a lot on luck as the rounds are so short that if you don't have the cards you need you have to waist a turn picking cards up and then you don't have enough turns left to do anything. 
The game has a lot of good points too, we enjoy the two phases to the game and resolving the actions in real time and we love the hidden rounds and special abilities. The game plays better with more players, I would say most fun with max player count. 
The next time we play I think we will add an extra round or two on the end with one of them a hidden round and see if it plays better. Jury's still out on this one.

RATING: 8
Meeples move up and down the 3D train based on cards you set down per round — with the randomness of the cards increasing as you get hit more, and your placements affected by the planned moves of the others. It's fairly simple and light on strategy, but the game is not meant to go long -- and, most importantly, the 3D aspect really helps to visualize what's going to happen which is something other games (like RoboRally) miss out on.

PLUS: theme, 3D visualization
MINUS: not a game that encourages deep thoughts

RATING: 7
Fun, family-friendly programmed action game. Does not have the length and complication of RoboRally. This is a much simpler game, for better and for worse. I enjoy this with my kids for the simple pleasures it offers, but there isn't quite enough variety here for an adult audience. 

I think the main reason I enjoy RoboRally more is because of the more challenging consequences to deal with when you are shot. In Colt Express, it borrows from deck-building games and adds useless cards to your draw deck. It is FAR more interesting figuring out how to negotiate locked programs when you are damaged in RoboRally.

RATING: 4
Un juego de programación de acciones.

Cada ronda los jugadores ponen cartas (boca arriba o boca abajo) sobre un un mazo común. Una vez que todos los jugadores han jugado sus cartas, el mazo común entra en juego. Cada acción que se muestra en las cartas se resuelve.

Visualmente, el juego es muy bonito pero tras jugar me quedé un poco decepcionado. Podría ser divertido, pero necesito más partidas para confirmarlo.
[color=green]
LAST PLAY: 2014
[/color][color=blue]
A game about action programming.

Each round players put cards (faced up or down) on a common deck. Once every player has played his cards, the common deck enters in play. Every action shown on the cards is solved.

Visually, this game looks amazing but I was a little disappointed after playing it. It could be fun but I need more plays to confirm it.[/color]

RATING: 8
Love it. So much fun to play, and evocative of the confusion of a train robbery full of untrustworthy characters. Getting a read on what people are planning to do and adjusting your tactics to react to them is intriguing - and especially surprising when someone takes a totally unexpected action in a tunnel.

Shares a frustrating aspect with other programmed movement games in that getting forced off your planned route can lead to turns where you effectively do nothing. But on the other hand, having a turn that goes totally cockeyed - but through some stroke of luck, still has you end up doing something productive - is hilariously entertaining.

RATING: 8
Really different and fresh feeling game with an unusually ambitious concentration on presentation. The train makes the whole game, and I love how there is a bunch of extraneous decorations (cactus, bones) to set on the table, with no effect on game play whatsoever.

The mechanisms are nothing new but they create excitement and wacky situations. If players are willing to play in a careless go-with-the-flow spirit, this should always go down well. If players are trying to memorize, calculate and optimize, it would suck the fun out. But as a quick, chaotic romp, this is wonderful.

RATING: 5
A programmed action game like a much smaller, much quicker, presumably more accessible Roborally. But the cramped play area also means that chaos is proportionally higher, the characters don't seem balanced at all, and the scoring system is just kinda off, both thematically and mechanically. There's also a palpable death spiral to the gunslinger element since getting shot slows your own rate of fire; therefore, if your power makes you much less likely to be hit... Definitely overproduced: the train could easily have been rendered flat in an isometric fashion and the stationary props only detract from the illusion of a moving train. Suspect I would still often choose this over Roborally.

RATING: 7
Programmed movement game on a train where bandits with asymmetrical powers are all fighting one another for bags of loot over several turns.  Everyone is also trying to avoid the Marshal, who is wandering through the train looking for the bandits.  The novelty of this game is that it is played in/on a 3D cardboard train.  Definitely clever and cute.  This was the 2015 Spiel des Jahres winner.

RATING: N/A
In Colt Express, you play a bandit robbing a train at the same time as other bandits, and your goal is to become the richest outlaw of the Old West. The game consists of five rounds, and each round has two phases:

Phase 1: Schemin' Each player plays 2-5 action cards on a common pile, with the cards being face up or face down depending on the type of the round. Instead of playing a card, a player can draw three cards from her deck.
Phase 2: Stealin' The action cards are carried out in the order they were played, with a player's best laid plans possibly not panning out due to mistakes and oversights!
The game takes place in a 3D train in which the bandits can move from one car to another, run on the roof, punch the other bandits, shoot them, rob the passengers, or draw the Marshal out of position. The train has as many cars as the number of players, and each car is seeded with gems, bags of loot or suitcases at the start of play.

FIRST IMPRESSION:

This was a charming and enjoyable romp.  Involves a bit of programming your actions, some of which you can see and some you cannot when programming is occurring.  As well, since you do not have your whole hand available, instead of programming a card you can draw three cards to enhance your options for the next programming opportunity.  Bullet cards are a pain as they will clog your deck and these can be received from other players who shoot you or from the deputy who is also happy to shoot you.  The characters also have special powers which are interesting but after first play, Belle feels a bit overpowered.

RATING: 8
[u]Comments:[/u]
Its rare that the first time I play a game I come away thinking that it was just flat out fun, Colt Express is one of those games. Programming games can be hit or miss with me, mostly on the miss side. Colt Express brings not only a compelling setting, but also very compelling artwork and components. The 3D train components are not only functional, but also pleasing to look at when set up on the table. The cardboard for the trains is extremely sturdy and should be able to withstand a good amount of punishment. The individual player powers are all very different and change the game up. All this and you add an extremely easy to understand rule set and you definitely have yourself a winner.

RATING: 7
I love RoboRally. When I play Galaxy Trucker, I never look at the event cards beforehand. Games in which you're hoping for everything to go horribly wrong are like music to me. So I liked what I heard about Colt Express and traded for a copy.

During our game I could see that the other three players were going to converge in a car next to the Marshall. I sneakily (it was a tunnel) played a "move the Marshall" card, excited to fill all three of them full of lead. However, all of them followed with Shoot cards. So when it came time for me to move the Marshall, if I'd kept to my plan, they'd all be on the roof firing at the only possible target: me. That's the kind of moment I love. 

There's some strategy here, and the winner certainly won through smart and well-timed card play, but mostly it's a lot of dumb surprising fun. I'm glad to have a copy of this.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Excellent game with very fun dynamics/mechanics.  Good for laughs especially if someone's well laid plans for a round are foiled by other players, and especially so when it happens multiple times in sequence.  Characters seem to consist of two good shooters, two good melee fighters, and two who are more nimble and well rounded.  

Plenty of strategies for winning, be careful not to let someone else's tactics sneak up on you.  One high value grab and it's over.  Game is fairly competitive, but the range of end results is wide (you can gain a lot or lose a lot in one turn, or stay fairly steady throughout).  Go with the flow and pay attention to how everyone's playing and make sure to use your own character's strengths to gain advantage.

Con: small train carriages makes for some difficulty moving pieces around.  Could be just 20% bigger to allow fingers to slide more easily into the carriages.  Ghost (white) seems slightly overpowered as I understand the mechanics currently, though I have only played two games, first as Doc (blue), then as Ghost.

Edit: All the comments from people who rated this game 4 or below either didn't follow the rules correctly or simply cannot plan, or guess, how other people are going to be playing cards.  Even if your "Schemin'" doesn't go 100% as planned you have to laugh, shrug, and get ready for the next round.  I get that it's frustrating to lose if you're a competitive person (I am too), but I hope they can grow out of it.  Try a different strategy and don't forget to use your character's inherent abilities while also watching out for other people doing the same (they will).

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
All of the chaotic fun of RoboRally without getting totally screwed over, with variable player powers, some more strategic planning (despite being a rather light game), and with a much more attractive "board".

The ability to sometimes see what your opponents are going to do allows you to better plan what you should do on your turn. On the other hand other people can still throw a monkey wrench via choosing who to shoot/punch, moving in the direction you didn't expect them to, etc, notwithstanding the tunnel turns where you place cards face down. Like RoboRally hand management is still important in this game as e.g. you only have one punch card.

I'm not completely sure how balanced all of the powers are, but they all seem fairly useful.

I definitely think this game works better in the higher player counts, as it gives more train space to move around. The more players there are the harder it is to keep track what everyone is going to do, but it also means you have a better chance of e.g. shooting someone just by sheer numbers.

One thing that might turn people off is since you can choose who you can shoot if there are multiple people in range, there is some take that aspect to the game. However, like I said above unlike Roborally getting shot even multiple times isn't the end of the world, and while it is possible to lose because e.g. someone chooses to punch you instead of someone else, it would be hard for someone to be in range to punch you repeatedly unless A. everyone just gangs up on you for no apparent reason or B. you are playing terribly.

Having said that, I'd love to play again!  Game play is definitely fun.

RATING: 6
This game is a lot like RoboRally but different in the following ways:
1 - Less space so you are bound to get in each other's way
2 - The game has a predetermined end (5 rounds, big plus)
3 - It is more focused on attacking then reaching a particular space on the board
4 - There is a marshall that affects everyone negatively

Cool components, although I suggest designating one person to move the pieces since it can get a bit crowded.

This game is silly, it is meant to be so and the enjoyment will be based on the group's attitude as much as anything.

playtime ~ 10 minutes per player

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
First programmatic game I ever played. Beautiful 'board' and components, great art and theme.
Impressions from playing 2 games:
- I like the programming and trying to deduce where I'll be. Or realizing I could be in one of two places, and trying to find an action that will work either way. Adaptation is key (especially since cards you draw may not let you continue the plans from the previous round). Theme was also fun.
- On negative side, Ghost character seems to clearly be the most powerful (came in 1st and 2nd, despite shuffling player-character pairs). This comes from the fact that hiding the first card they play can mess up several other players every round, while they can still compute everything (or everything minus tunnel; but either way it's a major informational and planning gain).
- Game lends itself to someone getting beat up on... at least happened in both games we played (e.g. getting shot 4 times in a row, 7 times in a round, despite being Belle). So not sure I would recommend this for kids (could get pretty upset). If you play multiple times, could even out. But I can see someone being virtually eliminated early on, which is not much fun,

Overall glad I played it, and will probably do so again sometime, but wouldn't buy it based on current impressions.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

It's a novelty, one that I would play again, but probably never purchase.

RATING: 9
Great chaotic programmed actions game with beautiful components and funny western theme. You're trying to rob the train but so are others. You put action cards in shared pile in turns (sometimes they're hidden), turn the deck around and see what happens -this is the fun part. It's pretty easy to teach (about 100x easier than something like Space Alert), interactive, fast and creates laughter. What more can you ask for? 

2-Player Comment:
*It's decent with two, slightly better than with 3. There's official 2p variant to emulate 4p chaos for two, it's not quite the same but there are fun times. 4-6 is recommended for intended fun though.

Expansions:
+Colt Express Playmat
+Colt Express Time Travel Car

RATING: 3
Update: Soured on it a bit after more plays, it gets stale and repetitive - while it was never difficult and the hidden cards / punch-cards make it impossible to predict perfectly there is never a (worthwhile) decision to be made.

This one was fun, and certainly a fair winner of the SdJ given the target market and complexity.

Programmable actions is fun, if only to prove that even the best laid plans will go awry. Every time. Even in rounds where every card is played open, something will undoubtedly go wrong, and it'll be a laugh for everyone even you.

I doubt the characters are particularly balanced if you were to play and re-play this title in a very competitive setting, but in a casual relaxed setting is where this game shines. Laughs and mischief abound.

I think this one will need expansions (and I can't see how it that won't happen) to stay amusing for many plays - but as a quick 20-40 minute game that plays up to 6 for great laughs, it's great! Yes, I'm repeating myself but bah.

A fine, or even good, game!

RATING: 9
This was a very enjoyable game! It feels like the big bad brother of Cash and Guns, which tends to get a little too simple. 

In this game, you have the same bunch of hooligans trying to get as much money as possible, but instead of a secret hideout you're in a much more exciting train in the Wild West, and you have roles with a special ability as well, and the injection of semi-hidden orders played out as if telling a story, making it a really exciting game. The component design is great as well, going full 3D and really getting you into the theme. 

And that's high praise from me, because I hate Westerns. 

Really really good game, am looking forward to acquiring it and its expansions for my collection.

RATING: 7.1
After a bit of a hiatus where, due to absences, transfers and resignations, my regular lunchtime gaming group only played two player card games (primarily Parade) one of our regular players (known in professional circles as Darth Lunch) returned to the fold and brought with him his new yuletide loot.

So far we've played this a couple of times and it has gone very well indeed. The set-up time and space requirements are a bit more than most of the games we play at lunch so we need a bit more time to ensure we finish the game but this is not an insurmountable obstacle. We got our second play down to the 40 minutes as described on the box so that's something.

So far Colt Express is a definite winner. The programmed moves work mechanic pretty well and it's a real hoot trying to anticipate what your opponents may be up to. 

We've only played with three so far but I'm pretty keen to try with more as that should add to the chaos (and the fun). It’s a rather nice touch having unique abilities for each character so each game is a bit different as you try to leverage your advantages to get the most loot.

A great little game, not one I’ll purchase but one I can see myself playing regularly over lunch.

RATING: 7
This game is pure fun! In the old west, program your moves one at a time, then solve them in proper order (First In First Out) to shoot each other, steal money and stay away from the Sheriff!
The more the players, the better; counting the bullets at the end of the round gives very funny moments ("So YOU shooted me 3 bullets, uh? Now wait MY lead, you gangster!").
At the core it's a very simple, fast game, highly accessible and a winner with large parties (4+).

RATING: 8
Wie es sich für ein "Spiel des Jahres" gehört, kommtColt Express mit übersichtlichen Regeln und einem leichten Einsteig für die ganze Familie daher. Doch Colt Express bietet auch für Kenner eine jede Menge Spaß, der Vergleich mit King of Tokyo bietet sich hier druchaus an: Jeder, mit dem ich bisher Colt Express gespielt habe, mochte es. Allein das Thema und die schöne Aufmachung sprechen schon für sich. Die Spieler sind Banditen im wilden Westen und wollen einen Zug überfallen. Dieser ist ein echter 3D-Zug, aus Pappteilen zusammen gesteckt - ein richtiger Eyecatcher. Das Spielprinzip ist einfach: Die Spieler haben ein Deck mit Aktionskarten (Bewegung, Schuss, Schlag, beute oder Marschal). Die Karten werden reihum gespielt, allerdings wird die Aktion nicht sofort ausgelöst, sondern erst am Ende der Runde, wenn alle Karten gespielt wurden. Man muss also darauf achten, die Aktion der Gegner zu verfolgen, um z.B. nicht ins Leere zu schlagen. Die Rundenkarten bringen Abwechslung, wenn z.B. manche Aktionskarten verdeckt gespielt werden müssen. Colt Express ist ein kurzweiliges, amüsantes Spiel. Für jede Gruppe zu empfehlen!

RATING: 8
Colt Express is a visually stunning game that evokes the 'Wild West Train Heist' beautifully. 

Combining RoboRally styled programming of actions each round (although implanted differently) the players try their best to form a plan and then watch as it goes awry. This element isn't quite as dramatic as it is in RoboRally however and doesn't feel quite as punishing. 

The aim of the game is to manuever around the train in order to collect valuable gems and bags of cash. Players can move vertically to access the roofs of carriages and horizontally to move through the train. This is important as the Sheriff guards a case containing $1000 at the front of the train and it is something of a race to get to it first. 

Of course players can also shoot one another and punch foes, which sees them drop a money bag. 

Throw in individual player actions and random round events to respond to and Colt Express is a really fun experience with an excellent time frame. 

Of the 3 SdJ nominees in 2015, this offers the most fun factor...even if that means that strategy meter is lessened.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Colt Express is a genuinely great game. Programming moves is nothing new in board games, but Colt Express manages to bring a new and exciting spin to it. It's almost like each player is writing the script to a play, just for their character. Then, at the end of each round, all four scripts are smashed together in the hope that things pan out how they wanted. This game could so easily have been designed on a flat board, but the 3d train is an amazing touch. It makes it so engaging and really helps players feel involved. This is probably my favourite 'board game', in the traditional sense. I'm usually more for party games, social games and a bit of bluffing/deduction, but this one perfectly scratches ever itch I want from a board game, and without a dice is sight.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Playing a bandit on a 19th century train, you preplan your moves as in Robo Rally.  You can move, climb up, shoot other bandits or steal loot. The trick is when you get shot it clogs up your hand with cards you can't use. There are various kinds of loot, and the best shooter gets a $1000 bonus. Whoever has the most money at the end of five rounds is the winner.

I'm not a fan of Robo Rally, so this game doesn't appeal to me too much. There are many things that can happen to you. For instance you start in the same caboose with another bandit, and someone else goes ahead of you in turn order and can punch you. Preplanning cards are played face down so you don't know what to expect. Some people like these kind of games. I just try to go with the flow. This was nominated for the Spiel des Jahres, so I was curious about the game. I would expect the chaos factor increases with more players and that could be funny, so this can be viewed as a light filler.

RATING: 7
A fun action programming game where you play bandits moving around on a train, stealing loot and trying to foil each other's plans. Each round, you take several turns playing actions into a pile (usually face-up, sometimes face-down), and then resolve all the actions in sequence at the end, so you have to remember what you or others have played and guess at the face-down cards. I really enjoyed the game, but my wife and daughter didn't like it as much.

RATING: 7.3
It takes the action programming from Roborally, even with the wounds that reduce your options, and puts it in a western theme and a superb looking 3D train.

Programming is much easier done here than in Roborally and there's more interaction, but there's [even] more randomness and you have less control.

There are balance issues with the character abilities: some are almost usless and some others are very good. The player that starts acting in the last turn gets a slight advantage.

Overall, it lasts a bit more than a filler should, but everything sums up to produce a nicely themed fun game, especially for those who are not into heavy gaming or whne you're in the mood for something very light.

RATING: 7.5
Partly programming, partly deck-management, but the large part a whole load of fun with some riotous characters and plenty of room to take the mickey out of people who misjudge their whole turn. Can comfortably play a large number in under an hour, which is always a boon too. 

The gratuitous 'extra scenery' is a generous and flamboyant touch which shouldn't be underestimated during a period when games publishers are nearly always looking to downsize.

RATING: 6
[b]Colt Express[/b] was sold via auction 11/5/15.
Received in a trade (6/1/15)

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]This game really took a nose dive after more plays. The amount of random chaos generated by the way program movement is handled in this game really left me wanting a game with a bit more control. The individual player powers were too unbalanced and I really disliked the "advanced" rules (you had to play through all your cards before selecting a previously played card) since it didn't do much to negate the random feeling of how the turns unfolded. Shocking that this one the SDJ, besides some really nice components this just isn't a game that I'd want to keep playing. I don't miss this one at all and neither do my kids.[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]- Colt Express is a great family game that deserves to win the SDJ.
- Amazing components, the trains look awesome set up on the table.
- Wild west train robbers and programmed movement is a perfect paiiring of theme and game mechanism.
- A breeze to teach, you can teach this game as you go. 
In this game the more chaos the better, so no worries if anyone makes a "mistake" since you never know how things will shake out.
- It is FUN! (In a hobby that can be so serious it's great to play a game that is not afraid to be a bit unbalanced, player powers really vary, and quite chaotic.)

This isn't a game that I want to play all the time, but it is fun especially when playing with family and friends. It also pulls people in once it is set up on the table and it can be taught easily, you will be off and running in no time. I highly recommend this game if you play with your family a lot, my guess is your kids will love it![/i]

RATING: 6.5
規則:
*火車使用跟人數相同節數，上面放對應錢袋(隨機抽)或寶物，警長放火車頭，照人數抽對應回合卡7取4洗勻放在火車卡3選1上，放13張中立子彈卡，起始隨機，基數玩家在尾巴火車下面格，偶數在旁邊格
*每人拿一腳色卡並拿250錢袋蓋著放上面，左邊放六張子彈卡，右邊洗勻10張行動卡蓋著，抽6張
*遊戲在五輪結束後，錢最多獲勝(子彈卡剩最少+1000元，平手都拿)，每輪有兩個階段，開始時開一張回合卡決定這回合出牌規則
1.出牌階段  照順序出一張牌開著形成牌庫(全部人疊在一起)，或是抽3張牌，回合數由回合卡決定
2.起始玩家拿走該牌庫，翻過來一張一張執行
>移動 下層左右移動一格，或是上層左右移動三格內，不能不動
>上下樓 
>移動警長 左右移動一格(當玩家跟警長同格時馬上移動道上層並拿一張中立子彈卡)
>開槍 下層左右一格可以射，上層則是直線上沒被檔到的，同格不算被檔
>搶劫 拿所在地的寶物一個
>打擊 打同格的人，並且他掉一個寶物在該車廂上，該人移動一格，
*每輪結束時所有牌(包括棄牌區)在洗勻，起始玩家順時針換人，進入下輪
腳色能力  1.每輪第一回合出牌時可蓋著出 2.打人時可偷錢袋，其他寶物掉地上 3.射傷他人時可以移動他 4.同車廂有其他目標時不能被打或射擊 5. 可同層車上下射擊 6.每輪抽7張卡
*回合卡 白面開著出，隧道格蓋著出，連續兩隔出兩張，反順位，對應事件在該輪結束發生
*專家變體*
*每輪結束沒用的手牌可選擇留或棄，拿到子彈卡要放到牌庫頂，牌不夠補6張時在洗勻棄牌堆
*兩人特殊規則*
*火車用四節，每人使用兩個腳色，牌庫所有腳色行動各留1形成11張的牌庫，每個角色有各自子彈庫跟腳色卡存錢，使用專家變體，最後比所有錢

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
The main draw of Colt Express is that it features a cool-looking three-dimensional train, on which the players move their pawns around picking up loot and shooting each other. Unfortunately, the gameplay is not particularly compelling. Players draw a hand of action cards, and play them one by one to perform actions with their pawn. Shooting other players gives them bullet cards in their action deck, which can limit their choices. The game is pretty much dominated by luck of the draw and multiplayer chaos, there’s really no coherent strategies. Players that happen to luck into some good loot will probably get beat back down by the other players. The game is a romp, and I guess that sort of thing has its fans, but I am not one.

(2 plays)

RATING: 8
This is rooting, tooting chaotic fun.  Wonderful components with the "board" being replaced by a 3D cardboard train. You play an outlaw trying to rob the train, but you are not the only outlaw out there.  Each player places their action facedown (or face up as the cards dictate) into a general pile.  Then, flip the pile over and move your meeple on the 3D train.  Moves are not the only action as you can pick up gems and moneybags; be shot or punched by other players, or be nabbed by the marshall. If you don't like games in which your best laid plans go awry, I would stay clear of this one. BUT....if you like to plan moves not really sure if they will come to fruition as well as play on a 3D train... man, this is simply fantastic
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Colt Express feels like a superior version of Bang! The Dice Game. 

The programmed movement mechanic works extremely well in Colt Express, and the ability to pick up the loot and make the other players drop the loot adds an extra dimension without the downside of player elimination.

The 3D train seems needlessly fiddly to me.  I would have been satisfied with a 2D board. Once you go 3D, the game seems to be begging for a mechanic where the cars become separated and the back of the train is eliminated.

RATING: 8
This is a game where you are a robber meeple with a unique power, running up and down a train robbing people and shooting other bandits. It was a ton of fun with 3 players, and I only see this getting better with 4, 5, or 6 players, as with 3 we were able to predict each others moves ~fairly~ accurately. This is an action programming game, where players either draw 3 or play 1 action from their hand in turn order faceup into a pile (unless the current event says you place it face down, which happens!), then you flip the pile over and resolve the deck from bottom to top. You do your best to anticipate where players are going and what they are doing, but for each time you get shot, you add a bullet card to your deck, which can clog you up on future draws, like wounds in Legendary or Curses in dominion. 

:star: Art, Iconography and components functional
:star: Clever or interesting mechanisms
:star: Reasonably low downtime between turns with mildly AP players
:star: Multiple plays stay interesting
:nostar: Low or mitigatable luck elements
:star::star::star::star::nostar: Raw enjoyment

RATING: 8
Fast paced, fun game loaded with social interaction, mistrust among players, and screw-your-neighbor good times.  The theme is well developed, and some of the mechanics brilliantly integrate that theme (particularly tunnels and swing arms).  Components are high quality, and the game has tremendous table impact.  Rules are intuitive and easy to teach.  
Colt Express is absolutely deserving of the praise and awards it has received.  It is a breath of fresh air in the board gaming world.

RATING: 6
This game scales very strangely with the number of players. With two players, each player controls two bandits in a team, but as you have to perform an action if able, you can end up shooting yourself in the foot semi-literally. Have so far only had the opportunity to play with 4-6 players. With four, the game is not too chaotic, as the number of cards being put into the game makes it somewhat feasible to track who is doing what, and to plan accordingly; the tunnel turns are what makes things tricky as cards start entering the schemin deck face down. With five people things get far more chaotic as by the time you get to throw in your next card you sometimes forget what you were doing beforehand. in one of my games someone was punched back and forth, and by the end of the round his dropped money had been picked up by the punchers, leading to a lot of whoop and hollering from the afflicted. With six players things get far more cozy as you start to get a lot more people clustering in the richer cars. The play is notably different with the number of players, despite the various scaling the game does with more players (really only an increase in the number of cars). 

The variety of round cards is nice (seven cards from which you draw four, with a final card taken from a set of three), but I wish there were more possibilities and combinations to give the game more of a chance of odd swings and events, such as end of round events taking place between turns in a round, rounds of all tunnel turns, or turns combining multiple turn types (speed-ups, tunnels, etc.). The game is a lot of fun especially with the right people. In the design journals for this game there is mention of how in earlier versions there were horses and other game elements; I can completely understand why they were removed as the game would likely gain little from added complexity, but at the same time it would be great to have a game with more stuff, ranging from horses to second trains to disconnected cars and dynamite.

RATING: 4
Short Version: didn't care for it. Played once and done.

Pros:
* The 3D components help the theme come out a bit.

Cons:
* Two player rules feel tacked on.
* Longer setup time.
* The 3D components make the game feel more fiddly. It is harder to move pieces around and pick up loot and it has a big impact on setup time. Honestly, I think I would have preferred a flat playing surface.
* We love interactive games with a healthy dose of "take that", but not when the interaction is frustrating. That's what this game is about. Each time you "interact", you are either completely disrupting that person's entire turn with little ability to take corrective action or you're making the next turn less fun.

= 2015-07-12

Finally got a chance to play this game yesterday. Not sure what I expected, but I don't think this was it. Having played RoboRally and Kings of Air and Steam, I was at least familiar with programming games and the "hilarity" of having your well scripted plan failing spectacularly, but this game managed only to distill that experience into frustration and boredom.

The two player rules were doubly frustrating in that you were less likely to get the cards you wanted to get a character into position. I suppose we could have burned more turns drawing additional cards, but that just feels like adding insult to injury; you already don't have the cards you need and now you have to give up precious actions to get them.

On top of feeling tacked on, the two player rules were also unheralded. We worked our way through the long and cumbersome setup process only to reach the last page and see *surprise* the two player setup is completely different! It would have been nice to have a more prominent notice informing us skip to the last page when playing with two (note: I wasn't the one reading the rules. If that noticed _was_ there, then I should be complaining about the rules reader instead of the author).

I have no idea how this game got nominated for the SdJ, let alone how it won. It wasn't horrible, but nothing about it said "game of the year" to me.

RATING: 8
Like watching an old western movie. Lol

.:Best 4:.

My Notes
Rule 1: Team Play
Pick your partner in crime. Team loot are added together including Gunslinger award. For example, one team has 2 shots for one and 2 shots for another but another team has 1 shot for one and 4 shots for another, the latter team gets the Gunslinger award!

Rule 2: Django
Django's shot, like a punch, makes the player drop loot on the car where they were shot. The player drops loot of their choice.

Rule 3: Tuco
Tuco's shot, like a punch, makes the player drop loot on the car where they were shot. The player drops loot of their choice.

Rule 4: Falling off
If a character is punched in or on the Prison Car/Caboose (i.e. last car), Locomotive, or Time Traveling Car, that character may fall off! Re-enter in the Caboose in the next turn opposite of the character that caused it.

Rule 5: Sacks of Gold
Whoever has the most sacks of gold gets $500 bonus.


--
Expansions
//The Time Traveling Car (TTC)

My Notes for TTC
Rule 1: Movement Activation
Use a die to indicate where the Meeple will be instead of players closing their eyes. When it is the character's turn, the player dramatically reveals the die for the location. lol

Rule 2: Shooting from the TTC 
Bandit in the TTC cannot shoot others on the roof of other cars but only to the locomotive. 

// Rock Promo - A place to put the cards.

// Marshal & Prisoners
My Notes for M&P
Rule 1: Mei
When using the Punch card, she punches the character to the roof or to the floor opposite of her.

Horse Card-  movement is one forward or any cars back. Then she needs to play a floor change card to get off the horse and it is her choice as to roof or into the car. She may only shoot adjacent to the car as well as other shooting her. 

Rule 2: Deadly Fall Card
If you punch a character on the roof, you may choose to knock that character off the train. The character returns via horseback in the caboose, the last car.

RATING: 5
Fans Of RoboRally, well you'll likely stick with RoboRally.

This game also uses cards to "program" what your Train Robber will do, but unlike RoboRally, You submit most every "command" in full public view one at a time, in turn order.  So Not only do you get to have the frustrations of drawing ineffectual command cards, but the one that might be worth a damn to play this turn are usually nullified by the cutthroat players who can take advantage of their turn order.  I'm not afraid of cutthroat, but I'm no fan of someone else being able to make my very few viable plays turn into inert plays.  In a four round game I spent 3 turns in the same car looting nothing, unable to move from the spot.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3.5
09-12-2014. Rated after 1 play. I never want to play this game again, but it has a good theme. In the game you're highway (wo)men attacking a train in order to obtain loot.

At the start of the round, all players play action card in turn order that allows you to move from left to right, up or down, or allows you to hit or shoot someone and importantly the action to obtain treasure. Some rounds cards are played face up, some face down depending on the round card. Player that gets rid of thier bullits gets a special bonus $1000, and there is a container that's worth $1000. Hitting people leads them to drop treasure you can pick up. In the cabin with the $1000 container a police officer hides that punishes you.

At the end, player with most treasure wins. I don't like the randomness, programmed movement nor the way you're rewarded if you just go gun-ho the whole time. Also, it's hard to control when a hit works.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Great, fun little game with over the top production values. It's fast playing and good for a few laughs. The wife has given this game her stamp of approval. We like climbing all over the train and punching each other in the face, shooting at people in the neighbouring carriage and all the while watching the tumbleweeds roll by in the distance as we get rich or poor.

Program three or four actions face up on a pile from your hand of six cards (which becomes increasingly muddied up with bullet holes as other players fill you full of lead). Then run through the actions. Do this for five rounds and the player with the most money wins. Easy to teach. Plays in 30-45 minutes depending upon experience. Lots of laughs, taunts and groans. There's a few extra bits that nicely spice things up, but that's the sum of it really.

As much as I like the production (and I do), I'd like to see this as a little card game version down the road. Yes the 3D trains really set the game up well, but it's really no more than an overproduced (in a good way), card game. A travel version in a small box would be ideal for my needs.

RATING: 6
The main fun in this type of game comes with the way actions can interfere with other players plans. 

* 3D model of the train is always a big draw

* Chaos for the interaction of player actions is fun

* Easy for non-gamers to leard

Two issues I have with the game are:

* Random card draws every turn mean that often you won't have the card you want. This is a bad experience for a new player who just has to toss in some random card

* Sometimes one player can end up at the other end of the train just collecting loot by themselves. While this is a good strategy to win, it can be a boring game for that person just sitting there without any interaction

The game is better with the expert rules where you have more control on the cards you draw. However, I'm mostly playing this game with non-gamers with the basic rules.
